<div id="review_257859997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257859997" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5064359-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324514114p2/5064359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257859997?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/5064359-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257859997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15876103344405204469">This is one of the worst Catherine Anderson books I had the misfortune of reading. Everything that plagues her style, mainly her penchant for unbelievably sugar-coated-and-then-dipped-in-honey heroes, is here magnified without any of the redeeming qualities of a gripping story (as in her far superior 'Annie's Song' and 'Comanche Moon'). The reader goes into an acute hyperglycaemia coma, with nothing to compensate for the boy scout hero. <br/><br/>Poor Ryan Kendrick! Not only does he not escape the typical</span>
  <span id="freeText15876103344405204469" style="display:none">This is one of the worst Catherine Anderson books I had the misfortune of reading. Everything that plagues her style, mainly her penchant for unbelievably sugar-coated-and-then-dipped-in-honey heroes, is here magnified without any of the redeeming qualities of a gripping story (as in her far superior 'Annie's Song' and 'Comanche Moon'). The reader goes into an acute hyperglycaemia coma, with nothing to compensate for the boy scout hero. <br /><br />Poor Ryan Kendrick! Not only does he not escape the typical Anderson hero treatment (perish the thought that a fictional character would remotely resemble the real men whose fictional form he is/should be)he's also chained to a tedious, irksome, humdrum and long drawn-out story. The super-hunk millionaire takes one look at the heroine (them big violet-blues wot did it) and he immediately knows this is the woman he's been 'waiting for' all his life. How does he know this? Why, she likes horses(apparently, she's the only horse-lover this play-boy, sought after bachelor, who's been around the block a trillion times, has ever met in rural, ranch-land Oregon),and something called a 'mud pull' (too boring to describe what it is) and, of course, hero and heroine also like the same song (bless!). Who could possibly remain unmoved by this enormous and profound affinity! These indestructible bonds of love are more than sufficient (in Anderson land)to make the hero sprint across the thousands of acres of his prime land, vault the pristine fences of his ranch and start redecorating his home and stables (more like rebuilding the whole blasted compound),while constantly crawling at the heroine's feet, begging her to let him be her lover/husband. Never once does our boy scout voice any fears about the difficulties facing a couple, where one is a paraplegic (that would be honest, and would interfere with the sugar-coat).<br /><br />I forgot to mention that the main reason the hero sites, in justifying his resolve to marry the heroine, is that he 'feels lonely' -something that contradicts Anderson's earlier descriptions of him as a sought after play-boy, with this tightly-knit loving family living just a few minutes away from him. So he thinks his life would be full of excitement and fulfilling intimacy, once he gets himself a person with a severe disability. The experience of families of people with severe disabilities is entirely the opposite of what the hero dreams of having(but, hey, he's a multimillionaire he can afford to employ an army of carers), their experience is that of an almost non-existent social life, of hard work just to get things to a functioning level, emotional turmoil, depression. Disability also makes a person so dependent on others that her/his only way of winning some space for herself/himself is to force that space and tenaciously patrol it. Loving a person with special needs means accepting that and letting go of the fantasies of perfect intimacy (one can only hope for a lovingly suffered distance). <br /><br />Another irritating point about all books of this kind is that you have these enormous families, with five, seven, eleven siblings and each one of them gets their own book, extending the formula ad infinitum. I think publishers should put a stop to this and demand that heroes and heroines be only children from now on. <br /><br />For the record, I got so bored with this book that I did not finish it, I gave up even before Ryan got to persuade the heroine to experiment in the bedroom. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15876103344405204469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1441130508" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441130508" />
    <a title="Cruth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12723605-cruth"><img alt="Cruth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392864210p2/12723605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1441130508?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cruth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cruth" href="/user/show/12723605-cruth">Cruth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/17015011-phantom-waltz">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=child-character">child-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=smalltown">smalltown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=hero-injured">hero-injured</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=heroine-injured">heroine-injured</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=christian-with-sex">christian-with-sex</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1441130508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2908843411189924240"><b>Author</b>: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/51304.Catherine_Anderson' title='Catherine Anderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catherine Anderson</a><br/><b>First published</b>: 2001<br/><b>Length</b>: 419 pages, 7574 kindle locations<br/><b>Setting</b>: Contemporary. Crystal Falls, Oregon.<br/><b>Sex</b>: Explicit. Reasonably frequent.<br/><b>Hero</b>: Multi-millionaire Ranch Owner.<br/><b>Heroine</b>: Paraplegic computer programmer.<br/><br/>On the plus side, this is a lovely, pure romance with no outside protagonists or vague mysteries to spoil the <i>getting to know you, getting to know all about you</i>. Strong, independent heroine who knows her own mind and strives against all odds. Sexy and virgi</span>
  <span id="freeText2908843411189924240" style="display:none"><b>Author</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/51304.Catherine_Anderson" title="Catherine Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine Anderson</a><br /><b>First published</b>: 2001<br /><b>Length</b>: 419 pages, 7574 kindle locations<br /><b>Setting</b>: Contemporary. Crystal Falls, Oregon.<br /><b>Sex</b>: Explicit. Reasonably frequent.<br /><b>Hero</b>: Multi-millionaire Ranch Owner.<br /><b>Heroine</b>: Paraplegic computer programmer.<br /><br />On the plus side, this is a lovely, pure romance with no outside protagonists or vague mysteries to spoil the <i>getting to know you, getting to know all about you</i>. Strong, independent heroine who knows her own mind and strives against all odds. Sexy and virginal. Protective hero, respectful and honourable. Rich and handsome.<br /><br />On the other side, though, is this slightly creepy cringe factor where Ryan is struck by <i>Love at first sight</i> and so, for the next few weeks, spends thousands of dollars buying equipment, paving the ranch, finding her horse, to make his ranch liveable for her <i>without Bethany knowing</i>. Romantic? Maybe, if he only added a couple of ramps and some bars. But completely rebuilding the kitchen?!? But apparently it’s fine because he’s rich and he has the money to spend and he’s in love and it’s all good. Sounds creepy to me.<br /><br />So overall a good, enjoyable story. An interesting discussion of the struggles of the disabled as well as the possibilities given the opportunities. But there are bits that make my eye squint.<br /><br /><b>Kendrick/Coulter/Harrigan series</b>:<br />Book 1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/89363.Baby_Love" title="Baby Love by Catherine Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Baby Love</a> -               <span id="reviewTextContainer139056545" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18004174392074459097">This was my first Catherine Anderson book and ...Wow, what a love story. Ryan Kendrick was so madly and truly in love with Bethany at first sight, he was her perfect knight in shining armor- and she needed one. They were both so selfless that I don't know who loved each other more because they both sacrificed so much for one another. He was supposedly such a player and I wish the author would have spent sometime on Ryan before he fell for Bethany because by the way he acted towards her I didn't </span>
  <span id="freeText18004174392074459097" style="display:none">This was my first Catherine Anderson book and ...Wow, what a love story. Ryan Kendrick was so madly and truly in love with Bethany at first sight, he was her perfect knight in shining armor- and she needed one. They were both so selfless that I don't know who loved each other more because they both sacrificed so much for one another. He was supposedly such a player and I wish the author would have spent sometime on Ryan before he fell for Bethany because by the way he acted towards her I didn't believe he was anything but perfect. <p>She had been a paraplegic for 8 years because of a horrible horse accident. She was happy on the outside, but slowly suffocating on the inside. Ryan rescued her from that existence and changed her whole life. After their first amazing date he updated his whole ranch (no problem since he had 50 million in the bank) to accommodate her disabilities, he was amazing. The story just moseyed along focusing more on life's challenges then any major conflicts. There really wasn't a villain unless maybe a wheelchair or a black bear. This was definitely a feel good story complete with a few choke up moments, a wonderful H&amp;h and some funny critters.</p></span>

<div id="review_196042257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196042257" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/667272-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376230788p2/667272.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196042257?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/667272-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/667272-christine?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196042257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12415254764209149786">I actually read this a few months ago, but wasn't sure how to rate it. I'm still not. On the one hand, kudos to the author for having a wheelchair-bound heroine. It's a refreshing change to the same old story all the time. <br/><br/>On the other hand...love at first sight is a tough sell, even in romance novels, especially when it is as extreme as it was in this case. We get the whole, "I've never felt this way with anyone before." And it's like why? How is this girl the right one for you? Because she lik</span>
  <span id="freeText12415254764209149786" style="display:none">I actually read this a few months ago, but wasn't sure how to rate it. I'm still not. On the one hand, kudos to the author for having a wheelchair-bound heroine. It's a refreshing change to the same old story all the time. <br /><br />On the other hand...love at first sight is a tough sell, even in romance novels, especially when it is as extreme as it was in this case. We get the whole, "I've never felt this way with anyone before." And it's like why? How is this girl the right one for you? Because she likes horses? You live in a ranching community, I have trouble believing you really couldn't find a few horse-loving women. Because you both like the same country song playing on the radio? That sounds like a very immature high schooler's definition of love. Maybe junior high. <br /><br />Ryan's great for her -- no question. He's rich and he has no qualms whatsoever about throwing his money after Bethany's special needs. He pours concrete paths around his ranch to make it wheelchair accessible, remodels his kitchen, refits his bathroom...he swoops in to be her knight and shining armor. But why? And I'm not saying she's not a nice person because she is, but it was too fast, too hard, and just too...random, maybe? How is she what he needs? <br /><br />Okay, look, here's another thing. Ryan is 30 and has been around. Bethany is 26 and a virgin. Since she was crippled at 18, that makes sense. Why she hasn't even tried a solo flight to see if things are working down there...well, her explanation made very little sense to me, but whatever. So Ryan won't make a move with a virgin unless it's going to be forever. His father beat it in his head that you only have sex with girls who "know the score." What the heck is that supposed to mean? Your cherry gets punctured and all of a sudden you have no feelings anymore? And why does he get to have sex with every woman who'll say yes in an attempt to find the right one but she had better be pure as the driven snow? <br /><br />Don't get me wrong -- this is very, very common in romance novels. But there were just a few lines in the story, especially the ones about knowing the score, that really, really bugged me. And here's why: He claims he's actively been looking for Ms. Right all this time, and that now he just knows this is the woman. He's tried many girls, but they never made him feel this way. Well...if you only ever tried girls who were (or who you stupidly believed were) emotionally uninvolved in making love, then DUH! Come on, who are you trying to kid here? <br /><br />I guess it's one thing to be a self-serving rake whose heart gets melted by the right woman when no other could before (which is still far-fetched) and another to be a supposedly nice guy who somehow doesn't understand that most women DO get their emotions involved with sex, whether they've done it before or not. <br /><br />I suppose you could not be looking for Ms. Right. You could, for some reason, be bound and determined to remain single and so you never hook up with a girl in a real relationship, only prostitutes or something. But you can't have it both ways. If you're trying to find a woman you could marry, and you're sleeping with them along the way, you're leaving behind a trail of broken hearts. There is no score to know here! <br /><br />Hmmm....I wonder if I needed to get that off my chest? :)<br /><br />It's not a bad book. If you already like Catherine Anderson, you may enjoy this. She does have some better book, though, IMO. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12415254764209149786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer810038669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6100452154880945784">Well! At first, I thought this one was a historical romance novel, so I bought it without thinking, finally it turned out to be a contemporary novel, but it's ok cuz I like to read that genre too . And actually, I read the translated version of the book, not the original, so I don't know if that could change my feelings or not. <br/><br/>This novel is good, in my opinion, it's not excellent but good enough. The storyline is good, the characters are good. It didn't have those scenes where your heart almost</span>
  <span id="freeText6100452154880945784" style="display:none">Well! At first, I thought this one was a historical romance novel, so I bought it without thinking, finally it turned out to be a contemporary novel, but it's ok cuz I like to read that genre too . And actually, I read the translated version of the book, not the original, so I don't know if that could change my feelings or not. <br /><br />This novel is good, in my opinion, it's not excellent but good enough. The storyline is good, the characters are good. It didn't have those scenes where your heart almost jumped out of your chest, it didn't have those intense moments that took your breath away, but it was a beautiful love story. You can find romantic moments in there, you can find tears and smiles, you can have everything you need in this novel if you're a desperately romantic person...<br /><br />But, it still has something not so real. Ya know, like, Ryan was supposed to be a tough guy, he supposed to flirt a round a lot before meeting Benathy, yes, a bad boy. But I didn't feel that side of him. He appeared too soft, too gentle, too generous and too kind, it was nothing like he had changed after meeting Benathy at all, it was like he was just that same Ryan from the beginning to the end. I felt a little bit boring becuz of that, I was expecting something more from him, something special...<br /><br />About Benathy, I don't have much things to talk about her. She was a brave woman. She lived and loved with everything she had, and that was great. I can tell I like her, that's all.<br /><br />Anyway, if you're a desperately romantic person, who is looking for something absolutely romantic to read, this book is for you. Reallity is not always beautiful in the way we want, so I think it's ok to live a while in a world where everything is pink and everyone have a kind heart. Engjoy the book! And thanks for reading my nonsense review =)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6100452154880945784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14857099756016682248">This was the first book I've read by Catherine Anderson and I adored every minute of it. Anderson's ability to create such memorable characters that pull on your heart strings is absolutely addicting and yes, I don't mind the bits here and there filled with silly sappy stuff. IMHO, ya' gotta love the romance genre to really appreciate her novels...otherwise, run for the hills. I've never read a romance novel where one of the leading characters was handicapped and I found her (Bethany) journey fa</span>
  <span id="freeText14857099756016682248" style="display:none">This was the first book I've read by Catherine Anderson and I adored every minute of it. Anderson's ability to create such memorable characters that pull on your heart strings is absolutely addicting and yes, I don't mind the bits here and there filled with silly sappy stuff. IMHO, ya' gotta love the romance genre to really appreciate her novels...otherwise, run for the hills. I've never read a romance novel where one of the leading characters was handicapped and I found her (Bethany) journey fascinating, heartbreaking, and eye-opening. I love what Anderson did with her leading man, Ryan. Some may call the story predictable, but to me, there were plenty of tender and original moments to keep spontaneity at the forefront. And oh my Lord, did Ryan keep things spontaneous while remaining focused on his ultimate goal - yowzers! <br /><br />My only complaint is just a few bits from the final chapters - Bethany, Ryan, and Ann seemed to do something completely out of character for each of them and it actually weakened the overall storyline for me and left me asking:<br />(1) why didn't Ryan's mom run after Bethany (during her moment of self loathing and weakness) as she realized Bethany would be abandoning the only man she ever loved? (whey Ryan was hospitalized in the end)<br />(2) it made no sense that Bethany would just totally freak in the hospital and decide to leave forever after everything she had experienced and revealed with Ryan<br />(3) it also made no sense that Ryan would not have come running after Bethany after being angry and hurt for a week or two, but NOT SIX weeks later and still claiming "to Hell with her" - oh please!<br /><br />Ok all that said, loved the ultimate ending, and still totally loved the entire story as a whole like the crazy romantic chic that I am. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14857099756016682248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13042506118421594225">Phantom Waltz was such an amazing book! I loved Rafe Kendrick in Baby Love but RYAN Kendrick was to die for! You got to love the Kendrick brothers! When Ryan first laid eyes on Bethany he knew he would marry her. Bethany was sweet, bubbly and didn’t let her disability put a damper on her spirit.   <span id="freeText13042506118421594225" style="display:none">Phantom Waltz was such an amazing book! I loved Rafe Kendrick in Baby Love but RYAN Kendrick was to die for! You got to love the Kendrick brothers! When Ryan first laid eyes on Bethany he knew he would marry her. Bethany was sweet, bubbly and didn’t let her disability put a damper on her spirit. At first she was hesitant to love Ryan knowing that she would be a burden to him. How could she ever satisfy him sexually? Ryan has a reputation for woman falling at his feet and could have anyone woman he wanted. She wouldn’t set herself up for heartache but Ryan only wanted Bethany, nobody else. For the first time in Ryan's life he met a girl who was perfect for him. When a Kendrick meets the "one" they'd stop at nothing to get what they want. Ryan knew that the only way to win Bethany's heart was to form a long lasting friendship. He’d move heaven and earth for Bethany and was determined to win her over. Their friendship soon turned into such a sweet relationship. <br /><br />It was so cute how Ryan would pick Bethany up in his arms and dance with her all night. And how he transformed his entire ranch so it was handicap friendly. I loved the scene when Ryan risked his life to protect Bethany from a Bear. The way Ryan loved Bethany despite her handicap was the sweetest romance I’ve ever read! After the barrel accident that left Bethany handicapped she never thought she'd experience love, marriage or motherhood. But thanks to Ryan all her dreams came true!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 0739417185" href="/book/show/16219314-phantom-waltz">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9594917-lindsey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468959283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4411948863885590534">In <i>Phantom Waltz</i>, paraplegic Bethany Coulter lives her life knowing nothing will ever be the same since her accident eight years ago that lost her the ability to move from the waist down. Soon, though, she meets Ryan Kendrick, a rancher who sweeps her off her feet and shows her how to really live again. Their life is not without it's challenges; is their love enough to keep them together?<br/><br/>I really enjoyed reading this book, the first one I've read where the main character is restricted to a wheel</span>
  <span id="freeText4411948863885590534" style="display:none">In <i>Phantom Waltz</i>, paraplegic Bethany Coulter lives her life knowing nothing will ever be the same since her accident eight years ago that lost her the ability to move from the waist down. Soon, though, she meets Ryan Kendrick, a rancher who sweeps her off her feet and shows her how to really live again. Their life is not without it's challenges; is their love enough to keep them together?<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading this book, the first one I've read where the main character is restricted to a wheelchair. It was really interesting to see how one has to live with a handicap such as this, and I enjoyed reading about a heroine who is not perfect, as it tends to be written in other books I've read.<br /><br />Bethany and Ryan's relationship was beautiful to read, in that though they instantly felt attracted to each other, they focused on becoming friends first before lovers. I really enjoyed the progression of their relationship and reading about how thy so completely adored each other.<br /><br />This is the second time I've read <i>Phantom Waltz</i>, and I think I loved it even more this ti e around. I'll definitely read it again, along with the others in this series. I definitely recommend giving it a chance.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5268110680966244693">This one was okay. It was different in that the heroine was in a wheel chair. I thought the hero fell in love too quickly. Less than a week and seeing her twice and he's telling her brother he loves her and plans to marry her? Maybe I should just put this under the fantasy heading instead of contemporary romance. Then the hero revamped his entire ranch with wheel chair access before he even knew they were going to get together. I mean I could buy that he knew pretty soon but this was too soon. A</span>
  <span id="freeText5268110680966244693" style="display:none">This one was okay. It was different in that the heroine was in a wheel chair. I thought the hero fell in love too quickly. Less than a week and seeing her twice and he's telling her brother he loves her and plans to marry her? Maybe I should just put this under the fantasy heading instead of contemporary romance. Then the hero revamped his entire ranch with wheel chair access before he even knew they were going to get together. I mean I could buy that he knew pretty soon but this was too soon. Also, that conversation with the brother was pretty girly. No man I know talks like that, especially with another man he barely knows.<br /><br />There were some lovely lines where he was telling her he loved her. I just would have prefered they come after a realistic relationship. Especially considering that she was handicapped and there was no way he knew what he was getting into long term in so little time. Regardless if the author told me "he'd been doing some research."<br /><br />Here again as in the first book in this series, it seemed like the book should be over then it went on. The pacing of some of CA's books is sometimes off for me. <br /><br />There are other of her books that I like better.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer946111026097787244">Beautiful story and rewarding to read. This is my all time favorite Catherine Anderson novel (besides Annie's song). I have read it over and over again, and recommended it to others. It tells the story of a handicapped woman that has shied away from any type of romantic involvements since a horse riding accident that paralyzed her from the waist down. She is first spotted sitting behind the counter at her family's ranch supply store, and a cowboy that thinks she is cute asks her out not knowing </span>
  <span id="freeText946111026097787244" style="display:none">Beautiful story and rewarding to read. This is my all time favorite Catherine Anderson novel (besides Annie's song). I have read it over and over again, and recommended it to others. It tells the story of a handicapped woman that has shied away from any type of romantic involvements since a horse riding accident that paralyzed her from the waist down. She is first spotted sitting behind the counter at her family's ranch supply store, and a cowboy that thinks she is cute asks her out not knowing that she is actually sitting in a wheelchair until she rolls back away from the counter as a means to turn him off... he takes it as a challenge to show her that he isn't a shallow guy... but doesn't have the intention of falling in love with her. I won't give away the rest of the story, but the trials and struggles they overcome together and the friendship and love they find is one of the sweetest and most heartwarming things I have ever had the privilege of reading. My absolute favorite part is when he gets down on his knees asking God for help after a devastating experience of trying to make love to her... I cry every time... don't worry... love conquers all!</span>
  <a data-text-id="946111026097787244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Beth Pearson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4205576-beth-pearson"><img alt="Beth Pearson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416960241p2/4205576.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/553769919?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Pearson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Pearson" href="/user/show/4205576-beth-pearson">Beth Pearson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4205576-beth-pearson?shelf=romance-had-sex">romance-had-sex</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer553769919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10020492403708948769">Once again, Catherine Anderson write a story without your typical perfect man and perfect heroine. Although the guy is pretty perfect, the lady is a parapalegic in a wheelchair. So while it is your typical paperback romance novel, it is different in that there are lots of considerations that don't take place generally. Health, safety, mobility, stereo-types,etc. are all part of the story. <br/><br/>Sex warning:<br/>In most (all?) of the stories I've read from Anderson, sex does not come until after marriage. T</span>
  <span id="freeText10020492403708948769" style="display:none">Once again, Catherine Anderson write a story without your typical perfect man and perfect heroine. Although the guy is pretty perfect, the lady is a parapalegic in a wheelchair. So while it is your typical paperback romance novel, it is different in that there are lots of considerations that don't take place generally. Health, safety, mobility, stereo-types,etc. are all part of the story. <br /><br />Sex warning:<br />In most (all?) of the stories I've read from Anderson, sex does not come until after marriage. There is definitely sex though and this book seemed to have a longer scene then usual based around the premise that the girl can't move or feel a lot of parts on her body so the actual ability to have sex was even questioned. Therefore, we have to go through a lot longer set up scene and then the whole what worked, what didn't. Parts were funny and parts were heart-felt. I don't know about the realism on the medical side of things, but liked the frank efforts on 2 very different people's desire to please each other. <br /><br />This wasn't in my top 3 favorite Anderson books, but I still liked the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10020492403708948769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201588717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3739734045177711073">Narrated by Julia Gibson<br/>The touching story of a paraplegic finding a man who worships her and is determined to make her life better, Phantom Waltz reads like a fairy tale at times. A DIK (A grade) when I read it some years ago, the listening experience didn’t rate as high for me. It may be the fact that narrator Julia Gibson is not a favorite of mine. Although the hero and heroine’s voice are usually clearly distinguishable one from the other, it is Gibson’s failure at timing and interpretation </span>
  <span id="freeText3739734045177711073" style="display:none">Narrated by Julia Gibson<br />The touching story of a paraplegic finding a man who worships her and is determined to make her life better, Phantom Waltz reads like a fairy tale at times. A DIK (A grade) when I read it some years ago, the listening experience didn’t rate as high for me. It may be the fact that narrator Julia Gibson is not a favorite of mine. Although the hero and heroine’s voice are usually clearly distinguishable one from the other, it is Gibson’s failure at timing and interpretation of events (that greatly differed from mine) that made the audio version less of a success than the original print book. The sensual scenes earn their hot rating but often sound a little too purple with terms such as “throbbing peak” or “tour of paradise”. Sound is the descriptive word here – I certainly wouldn’t want anyone to overhear these scenes as they sound a bit ridiculous at times.<br /><br />Written for the Speaking of Audiobooks column 6/17/10. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.likesbooks.com/blog/?p=4666">http://www.likesbooks.com/blog/?p=4666</a></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L4nYKvyNeiwR7ZOol9KeTo/lBwc3GBBDgYIpuQiUQFnejygeUYezcJtv0sy55tCXpgygonUV780m/QnZqtfu6Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  <span id="freeText12587727245419048762" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br />(1)romance author:<br />Adeline Catherine was born and raised in Grants Pass, Oregon, USA. She always yearned to be a writer like her mother. The morning that one of her professors asked if she could use samples of Catherine’s creative writing on an overhead projector to teach was a dream come true. In 1988, she sold her first book to Harlequin Intrigue and went on to write three more before she tried her hand at a single-title historical romance. Nine books later, she did her first single-title contemporary.<br /><br />Catherine married Sidney D. Anderson, an industrial electrician and entrepreneur. They had two sons, Sidney D. Jr. and John G. In 2001 she and her husband purchased a central Oregon home located on a ridge with incredible mountain views and surrounded by forestland honeycombed with trails. It was her dream home, a wonderland in the winter and beyond beautiful in the summer. She named it Cinnamon Ridge after the huge ponderosa pines on the property, which sport bark the color of cinnamon.<br /><br />Sadly, Catherine lost her husband to a long-term illness in 2014. She has kept Cinnamon Ridge as her primary residence but divides her time between there and her son John's farm, where she has the support of her loved ones and can enjoy his horses, cows, and raise her own chickens.<br /><br />Catherine loves animals and birds, both wild and domestic. She presently has two Australian shepherds, six cats, and a very old canary. She is very family oriented as well. Her older son has lived in Japan, Australia, and now resides in New Zealand. Catherine and her stateside family will celebrate Christmas on the north island with Sidney, his wife Mary, and their two sons, Liam and Jonas.</span>

Then, with perfect timing, a winsome red-haired woman named Ceara O’Ceallaigh mysteriously appears on Quincy’s property and insists that Loni can be cured. Only Quincy, she says, as the sole remaining Harrigan bachelor, can make it happen—by marrying Ceara. To Quincy, Ceara is a charming and quite likely deranged spinner of dreams who can’t prove she’s telling the truth. But how can he pass up any attempt to restore Loni to health? Against all better judgment, he decides to marry Ceara. Maybe he’s making the worst mistake of his life.
